My number one restaurant on the planet for her food alone, but the place offers an interesting variety of artifacts and trinkets from days past to feast your eyes on and remember days gone by.....I 100% recommend this place to everyone that has taste buds that enjoy being delighted.<//Review>

They are known for their embarradas de chicharron con chile which is a hand made corn tortilla with refried beans and handmade chicarrones con chile Verde. So delicious. He looked SURPRISED!? And he didn't even take all of it. He took two plates and left a dirty glass and didn't even wipe the table. After waiting another 10 minutes with no cleaning, place setting, and not even a self serve station to do it myself, I asked him to make it a To-Go order, and decided this will be my last meal there.

ORIGINAL: New and improved! This place reopened under new management with a fresh paint job, nicer interior, and much better food. The naan was some of the best I've ever had!< /review>

<text>The momo's taste the way my Tibetan ex used to make them.  Might be nostalgia, but I thought they were quite tasty.

Their onion naan and plain naan are exquisite.  Wasn't a fan of the potato stuffed one or the garlic naan, but I could tell they were well made.  Just not my cup of tea.  Pretty good lamb & spinach curry to go with it, no complaints there.

< Review>
Great little spot to get really fresh and delicious sushi. Nice little secluded spot near City College. Has a great atmosphere of modern and art. Seating ranges from bar tables to booths. Service is friendly and fairly attentive. Can get crowded since it has a small dining area but, easily looked past for the quality of the food here. Between the healthy serving rolls down to the sashimi. Hive definitely has a solid line up. Fish is fresh and delicious, preparation is timely and clean. Even better they are one of the few sushi restaurants that are open late. All in All highly recommend, easily would say give it a try.<//Review>

I went here for happy hour because I've been meaning to try this based on my coworkers & friends recommendations.

<name>Fernando Vivanco<//name><review>This felt a bit like playing Mario Odyssey, except there was no little guy to ask for directions. We had to find a table, collect soy sauce, chop sticks and soy sauce plates ourselves. No greeting as we arrive. Our waitress, Eneida, was very inattentive from the beginning. Did not even introduce herself or ask how we were doing. I understand if the restaurant was super busy, but there were only three other couples hanging out.

Not only food was delivered backwards (sushi, then won ton then oysters at the very end). But as many others reviewers already mentioned: the wait. We get like two pieces of sushi and then 20 minutes later another 3 pieces. After about an hour and twenty minutes my girlfriend started to fall asleep in the booth. I stood up and walked around the restaurant looking for our server. No one likes to feel trapped in a restaurant. We were digging up for cash so we could account as best as possible and just leave but we didn't have enough. I went to get a pen so I could write my address and they could bill me and that's when the waitress popped out of nowhere.

Not sure what happened with Eneida (Glydon), I think she was chillin' outside. Mario can take control of Glydon to glide and dive, however, when captured, Glydon is unable to swim and simply disappears as soon as he touches water!

I don't mean to sound hard and sorry if you were not having a good night. But we also worked very hard all week so we can enjoy the little time off we have and have a good time on a Saturday night.

We use to come here regularly for happy hour, from 10pm to midnight. Service and food was a lot better in the past. There were some good items like baked mussels. The sushi quality itself was pretty good for the price as well. Also, at one point one of the ladies in the kitchen allowed us to order the Monkey Balls dessert even though the kitchen was closed. However, during the last two visits I noticed the rice has always been hard and cold.

I can deal with the not so great rice but all it takes is one terrible experience to not ever want to come back again. I really hope the business owner reads through this comments and make some changes.< /review><user_id>108326220298676430752<//user_id>< Gmap_id>

<user>103807388213251279997< /user>< Name>
Tim</Name>
< Time>
1503685020443</Time>
<Rate>5< /Rate>< Review>
Among the more interesting sushi places in SD.

You enter from C street down some stairs like a New York dive or from the nectar room through 14th, which is newish (for years this front room was rarely used)

One of the head chefs (Tim) has been there going on 9 years, and most of the staff I've run into recently have been there for awhile (Ryan going on 1.5 years) so they know the regulars and the joint is clearly treating them well. Service is very good. Always has been.

The sushi is excellent. The availability of daily specials is always changing keeping things fresh. The rolls are gigantic and unless you are starving only one with a side is usually necessary. Speaking of sides, they are awesome. You have probably read reviews mentioning the monkey balls. There is good reason for that. Don't ignore the spicy garlic edamame either, it's the best I've ever had. Even if the sushi was average, I'd still go here for the edamame.

Happy hour is good, but the discount is really minimal ($1 off drinks, slight discount on sushi) overall it makes a difference of a few bucks to just reinvest into the tip.

Lastly, the selection of alcohol and beer is fantastic. The staff is intimately familiar with the beer list. Many of the staff here can be found at Hamiltons up the street after closing...Hamiltons having one of the best beer selections around. Ask for a sample if in doubt. Also, don't hesitate for a sake flight if you want a little drinking diversity.<//Review>

< Review>
3.5 stars

I'm a goody-goodie.

I don't drink, I don't smoke, I don't do drugs.

My only vice, other than my collection of human ears (Walking Dead) ;P, is gluttony.

Sometimes I do slip & get drunk.  Pizza drunk @ Goody's!

Goody's has coupons in the weekly Pennysaver for a large 1-topping carryout pizza for $6.99.  This sucker is large!  Around 15" in diameter large.  Today's choice of topping was bacon.

It's not artisanal, it's not made in a clay oven direct from the Italian peninsula, but it's not supposed to be.  It's cheap, greasy pizza that'll fulfill your moment of unhealthiness to a tee.

I walked in, ordered my pie & was told it would take around 10 mins.  Came back in around 7 mins & gathered my pizza, parmesan & pepper flakes to go.  I'm gnoshing on a slice now, if you can tell by all the greasy words in my review.

I haven't had their fried chicken in a long time, so I can't make an honest, up to date review on it.  Goody's also has pizza by the slice for those looking for a snack.

$6.99 large pizza?  C'mon, the pizza & the price = win/win!

Highly recommend w/ the Pennysaver coupon.

NOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNMONOMNOM<//Review>
